<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Vidya Balan</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">In this <a href="/wiki/Indian_name" title="Indian name">Indian name</a>, the name <i>Balan</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Patronymic" title="Patronymic">patronymic</a>, not a <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">family name</a>, and the person should be referred to by the <a href="/wiki/Given_name" title="Given name">given name</a>, <i>Vidya</i>.</div>

<p><b>Vidya Balan</b> (pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA for Hindi and Urdu">[ʋɪd̪jaː baːlən]</a></span>; born 1 January 1979) is an Indian actress. She has established a career in <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> and is the recipient of <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Vidya_Balan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Vidya Balan">several awards</a>, including a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Award</a>, five <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a>, and five <a href="/wiki/Screen_Awards" title="Screen Awards">Screen Awards</a>, and was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Shri" title="Padma Shri">Padma Shri</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> in 2014. She is known for portraying strong female protagonists and has been acknowledged in the media for pioneering a change in the concept of a Hindi film heroine.</p>
<p>Vidya aspired to a career in film from a young age, and had her first acting role in the 1995 sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_Paanch_(TV_series)" title="Hum Paanch (TV series)">Hum Paanch</a></i>. She pursued a master's degree in <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mumbai" title="University of Mumbai">University of Mumbai</a> and simultaneously made several unsuccessful attempts to start a career in film. She subsequently featured in various television commercials and music videos, and in 2003 made her feature film debut as the protagonist of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_West_Bengal" title="Cinema of West Bengal">Bengali</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Bhalo_Theko" title="Bhalo Theko">Bhalo Theko</a></i>. In 2005 Vidya garnered praise for her first Hindi film, the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Parineeta_(2005_film)" title="Parineeta (2005 film)">Parineeta</a></i>, and followed it with a leading role in the highly successful 2006 comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Lage_Raho_Munna_Bhai" title="Lage Raho Munna Bhai">Lage Raho Munna Bhai</a></i>.</p>
<p>This initial success was followed by roles in the <a href="/wiki/Romantic_comedy_film" title="Romantic comedy film">romantic comedies</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Heyy_Babyy" title="Heyy Babyy">Heyy Babyy</a></i> (2007) and <i><a href="/wiki/Kismat_Konnection" title="Kismat Konnection">Kismat Konnection</a></i> (2008) which met with negative reviews. By 2009 Vidya had established herself as a leading actress of Hindi cinema, as she went on to portray five consecutive roles to wide critical acclaim in the 2009 drama <i><a href="/wiki/Paa_(film)" title="Paa (film)">Paa</a></i>, the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Black_comedy" title="Black comedy">black comedy</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Ishqiya" title="Ishqiya">Ishqiya</a></i>, the 2011 semi-biographical thriller <i><a href="/wiki/No_One_Killed_Jessica" title="No One Killed Jessica">No One Killed Jessica</a></i>, the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Biographical_film" title="Biographical film">biopic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dirty_Picture" title="The Dirty Picture">The Dirty Picture</a></i>, and the 2012 thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Kahaani" title="Kahaani">Kahaani</a></i>. She followed this with a series of films that performed poorly at the box office, although her performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Kahaani_2:_Durga_Rani_Singh" title="Kahaani 2: Durga Rani Singh">Kahaani 2: Durga Rani Singh</a></i> (2016) was praised.</p>
<p>In addition to acting in films, Vidya promotes humanitarian causes and supports the empowerment of women. She initially drew criticism for her fluctuating weight and "questionable" dress sense, but was later credited in the media for "not morphing herself to fit into any conventional slot".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quote1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-quote1-1">[1]</a></sup> She is married to the film producer <a href="/wiki/Siddharth_Roy_Kapur" title="Siddharth Roy Kapur">Siddharth Roy Kapur</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_background">Early life and background</span></h2>
<p>Vidya Balan was born on 1 January 1979 in <a href="/wiki/Chembur" title="Chembur">Chembur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> to parents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_people" title="Tamil people">Tamilian</a> descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Her father, P. R. Balan, is the executive vice-president of Digicable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and her mother, Saraswathy Balan, is a homemaker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-something_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-something-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> According to Vidya, they speak a mix of <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Her elder sister, Priya Balan, works in the field of advertising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-something_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-something-5">[5]</a></sup> The actress <a href="/wiki/Priyamani" title="Priyamani">Priyamani</a> is her second cousin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya grew up in the suburban neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/Chembur" title="Chembur">Chembur, Mumbai</a> and was schooled at St. Anthony Girls' High School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> From a young age she aspired to a career in film and was inspired by the work of actors <a href="/wiki/Shabana_Azmi" title="Shabana Azmi">Shabana Azmi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madhuri_Dixit" title="Madhuri Dixit">Madhuri Dixit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> At the age of sixteen, she starred in the first season of <a href="/wiki/Ekta_Kapoor" title="Ekta Kapoor">Ekta Kapoor</a>'s sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_Paanch_(TV_series)" title="Hum Paanch (TV series)">Hum Paanch</a></i> as Radhika, a bespectacled teenager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tree_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-tree-15">[15]</a></sup> Following the success of the show, Vidya refused director <a href="/wiki/Anurag_Basu" title="Anurag Basu">Anurag Basu</a>'s offer to star in a television soap opera, as she wanted to concentrate on a film career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-native_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-native-16">[16]</a></sup> Her parents were supportive of the decision but encouraged her to complete her education first,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> so she attended <a href="/wiki/St._Xavier%27s_College,_Mumbai" title="St. Xavier's College, Mumbai">St. Xavier's College</a> to pursue a bachelor's degree in <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> and later earned a master's degree from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mumbai" title="University of Mumbai">University of Mumbai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_and_film_debut_.282000.E2.80.9304.29">Struggle and film debut (2000–04)</span></h3>
<p>While pursuing her master's degree, Vidya was cast as the female lead in the <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">Malayalam film</a> <i>Chakram</i>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Mohanlal" title="Mohanlal">Mohanlal</a> and was subsequently signed on for twelve other Malayalam language films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> However, due to production difficulties, <i>Chakram</i> was shelved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beginning_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-beginning-19">[19]</a></sup> The postponement of a film starring Mohanlal was an unheard of occurrence in Malayalam cinema and film producers blamed Vidya for bringing "bad luck" to the project; labelled her as a "jinx" and replaced her in all the films that she had been contracted for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> She then shifted focus to <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">Tamil cinema</a>. In 2001, she was cast as the female lead in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N._Linguswamy" title="N. Linguswamy">N. Linguswamy</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Run_(2002_film)" title="Run (2002 film)">Run</a></i> (2002). However, after completing the first <a href="/wiki/Shooting_schedule" title="Shooting schedule">shooting schedule</a> of the film, she was unceremoniously dropped and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Meera_Jasmine" title="Meera Jasmine">Meera Jasmine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> She was signed up under false pretences for a <a href="/wiki/Sex_comedy" title="Sex comedy">sex comedy</a>, a genre she was then uncomfortable with, and thus decided to leave the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> Thereafter, she signed on for a third Tamil film, <i><a href="/wiki/Manasellam" title="Manasellam">Manasellam</a></i> (2003), but was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Trisha_(actress)" title="Trisha (actress)">Trisha</a> as the director was dissatisfied with her work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Kalari_Vikraman" title="Kalari Vikraman">Kalari Vikraman</a></i>, another Malayalam film that she completed work for in 2003, failed to get a theatrical release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>After failing to start a film career, Vidya appeared in approximately sixty television commercials and in music videos for <a href="/wiki/Euphoria_(Indian_band)" title="Euphoria (Indian band)">Euphoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shubha_Mudgal" title="Shubha Mudgal">Shubha Mudgal</a>; a majority of these were directed by <a href="/wiki/Pradeep_Sarkar" title="Pradeep Sarkar">Pradeep Sarkar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-native_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-native-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 2003, she was signed on by <a href="/wiki/Goutam_Halder" title="Goutam Halder">Goutam Halder</a> for his independent <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_West_Bengal" title="Cinema of West Bengal">Bengali</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Bhalo_Theko" title="Bhalo Theko">Bhalo Theko</a></i>; her first film release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Her portrayal of Anandi, a young woman reminiscing about her past, won her an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anandalok_Awards" title="Anandalok Awards">Anandalok Purashkar</a> for Best Actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakthrough_.282005.E2.80.9308.29">Breakthrough (2005–08)</span></h3>
<p>In 2005 Vidya made her Hindi film debut with Pradeep Sarkar's musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Parineeta_(2005_film)" title="Parineeta (2005 film)">Parineeta</a></i>. Before being cast for the film, she had to undergo extensive auditions for a period of six months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beginning_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-beginning-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The film, an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Sarat_Chandra_Chattopadhyay" title="Sarat Chandra Chattopadhyay">Sarat Chandra Chattopadhyay</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Parineeta" title="Parineeta">novel of the same name</a>, narrated the love story of an idealist Lalita (Vidya) and a musician Shekhar (<a href="/wiki/Saif_Ali_Khan" title="Saif Ali Khan">Saif Ali Khan</a>), the son of a capitalist businessman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Her performance in the film was praised by critics;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tree_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-tree-15">[15]</a></sup> Derek Elley from <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> wrote, "An acting revelation is Tamil newcomer [Vidya] Balan, whose devoted but dignified Lalita is the picture's heart and soul."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <i>Parineeta</i> fetched her a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filmfare_Best_Female_Debut_Award" title="Filmfare Best Female Debut Award">Best Female Debut</a> award and a nomination for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filmfare_Best_Actress_Award" title="Filmfare Best Actress Award">Best Actress</a> at the annual <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldawards_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-oldawards-29">[29]</a></sup> The following year, Vidya appeared opposite <a href="/wiki/Sanjay_Dutt" title="Sanjay Dutt">Sanjay Dutt</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Hirani" title="Rajkumar Hirani">Rajkumar Hirani</a>'s comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Lage_Raho_Munna_Bhai" title="Lage Raho Munna Bhai">Lage Raho Munna Bhai</a></i>. She portrayed the role of Jhanvi, a <a href="/wiki/Radio_personality" title="Radio personality">radio jockey</a> and the love interest of the protagonist <a href="/wiki/Munna_Bhai" title="Munna Bhai">Munna Bhai</a>. To prepare for her role, she met with a couple of radio jockeys and watched them at work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindusiddiqui_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindusiddiqui-30">[30]</a></sup> Her performance was critically well received,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and the film emerged as a <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">blockbuster</a> with earnings of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1.19 billion</span> (US$18 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all-time_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-all-time-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007 Vidya featured in a supporting role in <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a>'s semi-biographical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_(2007_film)" title="Guru (2007 film)">Guru</a></i> as a woman suffering from <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>. The film, which starred <a href="/wiki/Mithun_Chakraborty" title="Mithun Chakraborty">Mithun Chakraborty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Bachchan" title="Abhishek Bachchan">Abhishek Bachchan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aishwarya_Rai_Bachchan" title="Aishwarya Rai Bachchan">Aishwarya Rai Bachchan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R._Madhavan" title="R. Madhavan">R. Madhavan</a> in leading roles, performed well at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifetime_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime-33">[33]</a></sup> However, film critics <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Mohamed" title="Khalid Mohamed">Khalid Mohamed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raja_Sen" title="Raja Sen">Raja Sen</a> noted that her "talent was wasted" in a "minuscule role".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Her next release was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikhil_Advani" title="Nikhil Advani">Nikhil Advani</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salaam-e-Ishq:_A_Tribute_To_Love" title="Salaam-e-Ishq: A Tribute To Love">Salaam-e-Ishq: A Tribute To Love</a></i>, a romantic comedy featuring an <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a>, in which she was paired opposite <a href="/wiki/John_Abraham_(actor)" title="John Abraham (actor)">John Abraham</a>. The film, which narrated six individual love stories, saw Vidya play the role of a television reporter, Tehzeeb Hussain, suffering from a <a href="/wiki/Amnesia" title="Amnesia">memory loss condition</a>. The film, which was a critical and commercial failure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifetime_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime-33">[33]</a></sup> generated positive reviews for Vidya. Sukanya Verma of <a href="/wiki/Rediff.com" title="Rediff.com">Rediff.com</a> wrote, "Vidya's transformation from a self-assured working woman to a helpless, vulnerable person is superb."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_2008.jpeg"><img alt="Vidya Balan is looking directly at the camera." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="490" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Vidya_2008.jpeg/220px-Vidya_2008.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Vidya_2008.jpeg/330px-Vidya_2008.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Vidya_2008.jpeg/440px-Vidya_2008.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_2008.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vidya at a promotional event for <i><a href="/wiki/Bhool_Bhulaiyaa" title="Bhool Bhulaiyaa">Bhool Bhulaiyaa</a></i> in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vidya then took a supporting role in <a href="/wiki/Vidhu_Vinod_Chopra" title="Vidhu Vinod Chopra">Vidhu Vinod Chopra</a>'s drama <i><a href="/wiki/Eklavya:_The_Royal_Guard" title="Eklavya: The Royal Guard">Eklavya: The Royal Guard</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan" title="Amitabh Bachchan">Amitabh Bachchan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boman_Irani" title="Boman Irani">Boman Irani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharmila_Tagore" title="Sharmila Tagore">Sharmila Tagore</a>, Saif Ali Khan, and Sanjay Dutt. The film, which failed commercially, met with positive critical reviews and was selected as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_submissions_for_the_Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="List of Indian submissions for the Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">India's official entry to the Oscars</a> for the <a href="/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards" title="80th Academy Awards">80th Academy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> She was later cast as Isha Sahni, a single mother, in <a href="/wiki/Sajid_Khan_(director)" title="Sajid Khan (director)">Sajid Khan</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Heyy_Babyy" title="Heyy Babyy">Heyy Babyy</a></i>, alongside co-stars <a href="/wiki/Akshay_Kumar" title="Akshay Kumar">Akshay Kumar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ritesh_Deshmukh" title="Ritesh Deshmukh">Ritesh Deshmukh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fardeen_Khan" title="Fardeen Khan">Fardeen Khan</a>. The comedy film was a box-office success,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifetime_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime-33">[33]</a></sup> but garnered negative reviews from critics, as did Vidya's performance; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN-IBN" title="CNN-IBN">CNN-IBN</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rajeev_Masand" title="Rajeev Masand">Rajeev Masand</a> criticised her wardrobe and make-up, and considered her the "sore thumb" of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Publishing2008_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Publishing2008-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya's fifth and final film of 2007 was <a href="/wiki/Priyadarshan" title="Priyadarshan">Priyadarshan</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Bhool_Bhulaiyaa" title="Bhool Bhulaiyaa">Bhool Bhulaiyaa</a></i>, a remake of the Malayalam film <i><a href="/wiki/Manichitrathazhu" title="Manichitrathazhu">Manichitrathazhu</a></i> (1993). Vidya featured as Avani Chaturvedi (a character played by <a href="/wiki/Shobana" title="Shobana">Shobana</a> in the Malayalam original), a woman suffering from <a href="/wiki/Dissociative_identity_disorder" title="Dissociative identity disorder">dissociative identity disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Co-starring <a href="/wiki/Shiney_Ahuja" title="Shiney Ahuja">Shiney Ahuja</a>, Akshay Kumar, and <a href="/wiki/Ameesha_Patel" title="Ameesha Patel">Ameesha Patel</a>, <i>Bhool Bhulaiyaa</i> was a commercial success with a worldwide revenue of over <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>830 million</span> (US$12 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifetime_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-lifetime-33">[33]</a></sup> Reviewers, while being generally negative of the film, were appreciative of Vidya's performance. Writing for <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Times" title="Hindustan Times">Hindustan Times</a></i>, Khalid Mohamed described her as "bankably likeable" and <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Taran_Adarsh" title="Taran Adarsh">Taran Adarsh</a> labelled her as "splendid".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The role earned Vidya a second Filmfare nomination in the Best Actress category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldawards_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-oldawards-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008's <i><a href="/wiki/Halla_Bol" title="Halla Bol">Halla Bol</a></i>, Vidya played a supporting role alongside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ajay_Devgn" title="Ajay Devgn">Ajay Devgn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pankaj_Kapur" title="Pankaj Kapur">Pankaj Kapur</a>. The film was based on the life of activist <a href="/wiki/Safdar_Hashmi" title="Safdar Hashmi">Safdar Hashmi</a>, who was killed by political rivals while performing on a street play (by the name of <i>Halla Bol</i>) in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The film was a critical failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Later that year, she co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Shahid_Kapoor" title="Shahid Kapoor">Shahid Kapoor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aziz_Mirza" title="Aziz Mirza">Aziz Mirza</a>'s romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Kismat_Konnection" title="Kismat Konnection">Kismat Konnection</a></i>. Faring poorly at the box office,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> the film and her performance generated a negative response; critic Sonia Chopra commented, "[Balan] is made to look downright drab. The haircut is unflattering, the make-up too plain, the clothes usually in off-white or brown. Plus the character is repetitive and reminds us of the one she played in <i>Lage Raho Munna Bhai</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Widespread_success_.282009.E2.80.9312.29">Widespread success (2009–12)</span></h3>
<p>In 2009 Vidya played the role of an unwed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gynaecologist" title="Gynaecologist">gynaecologist</a> struggling with her 12-year-old son's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progeria_syndrome" title="Progeria syndrome">progeria syndrome</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/R._Balki" title="R. Balki">R. Balki</a>-directed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dramedy" title="Dramedy">dramedy</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Paa_(film)" title="Paa (film)">Paa</a></i>. Amitabh Bachchan played the role of Vidya's son and Abhishek Bachchan played the title character. A critical and commercial success, the film has been described as a major turning point in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Sukanya Verma compared her acting style to that of <a href="/wiki/Dimple_Kapadia" title="Dimple Kapadia">Dimple Kapadia</a> and noted, "Balan is poignant yet restrained and projects an impressive figure of grace and integrity";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nikhat_Kazmi" title="Nikhat Kazmi">Nikhat Kazmi</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i> further argued that Vidya was successful in lending a "rare dignity to the image of the Bollywood mom."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Her portrayal garnered her several awards, including a Filmfare Award for Best Actress and a <a href="/wiki/Screen_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Screen Award for Best Actress">Screen Award for Best Actress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldawards_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-oldawards-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya followed the success of <i>Paa</i> with the <a href="/wiki/Vishal_Bhardwaj" title="Vishal Bhardwaj">Vishal Bhardwaj</a>-produced <i><a href="/wiki/Ishqiya" title="Ishqiya">Ishqiya</a></i> (2010), a <a href="/wiki/Black_comedy" title="Black comedy">black comedy</a> directed by debutant <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Chaubey" title="Abhishek Chaubey">Abhishek Chaubey</a>; co-starring <a href="/wiki/Naseeruddin_Shah" title="Naseeruddin Shah">Naseeruddin Shah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arshad_Warsi" title="Arshad Warsi">Arshad Warsi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salman_Shahid" title="Salman Shahid">Salman Shahid</a>. Vidya's role was that of Krishna Verma, a sexually manipulative woman. Vidya described her character as "an epitome of grey" and a departure from the conventional portrayal of women in cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In preparation for her part, she undertook professional training to speak in the local <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>-dialect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The feature as well as her performance received critical acclaim; <a href="/wiki/Anupama_Chopra" title="Anupama Chopra">Anupama Chopra</a> of <a href="/wiki/NDTV" title="NDTV">NDTV</a> stated, "Vidya Balan's smoldering looks scorch the screen even as her eyes hint at tragedy. She proves that she is miles ahead of the cookie cutter Barbie dolls that clutter Bollywood and that sensuality has very little to do with showing skin."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Her work in the film earned Vidya a <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Critics_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actress">Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actress</a>, a second consecutive Best Actress award at Screen and a nomination for Best Actress at Filmfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awards_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-awards-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tusshar_Kapoor,_Vidya_Balan,_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_(10).jpg"><img alt="Tusshar Kapoor, Vidya Balan and Emraan Hashmi pose for the camera together." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="439" data-file-width="585" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg/220px-Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg/330px-Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg/440px-Tusshar_Kapoor%2C_Vidya_Balan%2C_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_%2810%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tusshar_Kapoor,_Vidya_Balan,_Emraan_Hashmi_at_The_Dirty_Picture_audio_release_(10).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vidya with co-stars <a href="/wiki/Tusshar_Kapoor" title="Tusshar Kapoor">Tusshar Kapoor</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Emraan_Hashmi" title="Emraan Hashmi">Emraan Hashmi</a> at the audio release of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Dirty_Picture_(2011_film)" title="The Dirty Picture (2011 film)">The Dirty Picture</a></i> in 2011. Her performance earned her a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="National Film Award for Best Actress">National Film Award for Best Actress</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actress">Filmfare Award for Best Actress</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Raj_Kumar_Gupta" title="Raj Kumar Gupta">Raj Kumar Gupta</a>'s semi-biographical thriller <i><a href="/wiki/No_One_Killed_Jessica" title="No One Killed Jessica">No One Killed Jessica</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Rani_Mukerji" title="Rani Mukerji">Rani Mukerji</a> was Vidya's first release of 2011. The film, based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jessica_Lal" title="Jessica Lal">Jessica Lal</a> murder case, saw her portray the real-life character of Sabrina Lal, Jessica's reticent sister. While preparing for the role, Vidya did not meet Lal on the insistence of Gupta as "the Sabrina [...] today is different from the Sabrina a decade ago, [when] the story begins".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <i>No One Killed Jessica</i> met with contrasting reviews from critics, but Vidya's performance was particularly praised. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> remarked on Vidya's ability to be "in sublime control over her emotions"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and Savera Someshwar of Rediff.com added that "her hesitant body language, her faith, her helplessness, her rage, her sorrow and her gratitude all come across beautifully".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The film had earnings of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>490 million</span> (US$7.3 million) and was noted for being a commercial success despite the absence of a male lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice2011_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice2011-58">[58]</a></sup> Vidya earned another Filmfare nomination in the Best Actress category for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In March 2011, a retrospective of Vidya's films was held in Australia, as part of the film festival <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_and_Beyond" title="Bollywood and Beyond">Bollywood &amp; Beyond</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> That same year, Vidya featured in a <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearance</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santosh_Sivan" title="Santosh Sivan">Santosh Sivan</a>'s Malayalam language <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Urumi_(film)" title="Urumi (film)">Urumi</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya's next appearance was in Ekta Kapoor's production <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Dirty_Picture_(2011_film)" title="The Dirty Picture (2011 film)">The Dirty Picture</a></i>, a biopic based on the life and death of the controversial Indian actress <a href="/wiki/Silk_Smitha" title="Silk Smitha">Silk Smitha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Vidya was cast as Silk, who was—in Vidya's words—"known for her brazenness and in-your-face sexuality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> She described the role as the "boldest" she had ever played, one that "required a lot of mental preparation," and to look the part, she gained 12 kilograms (26 lb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The film opened to major critical acclaim, and Vidya received unanimous praise for her portrayal which several reviewers regarded as her best performance to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hero_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hero-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Khalid Mohamed observed, "She's extraordinary: gutsy, consistently in character and unafraid of exposing her darker side. Here's the kind of complex performance which you haven't evidenced in years and years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Her director <a href="/wiki/Milan_Luthria" title="Milan Luthria">Milan Luthria</a> described her as the contemporary claimant of the "sex-symbol" title, and compared her "voluptuousness" to the likes of yesteryear actresses <a href="/wiki/Sridevi" title="Sridevi">Sridevi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vyjayanthimala" title="Vyjayanthimala">Vyjayanthimala</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The film was eventually declared a blockbuster, earning <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1.14 billion</span> (US$17 million) worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all-time_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-all-time-32">[32]</a></sup> Vidya won a second Filmfare Award, a third consecutive Screen Award, and a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="National Film Award for Best Actress">National Film Award for Best Actress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awards_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-awards-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-national_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-national-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>For her next feature film, Vidya starred as Vidya Bagchi, a pregnant woman in search of her missing husband in <a href="/wiki/Sujoy_Ghosh" title="Sujoy Ghosh">Sujoy Ghosh</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kahaani" title="Kahaani">Kahaani</a></i> (2012). The thriller, set in the city of <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Durga_Puja" title="Durga Puja">Durga Puja</a> festivities, met with wide critical acclaim. To lend authenticity to her part, Vidya met several pregnant women and learnt about their lifestyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> She generated public and media attention by wearing a fake baby bump during the film's promotional activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Vidya received further appreciation for her performance in <i>Kahaani</i>. Subhash K. Jha praised Vidya's portrayal of "grace under pressure" as "measured and skilled"; Pratim D. Gupta of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Telegraph_(Calcutta)" title="The Telegraph (Calcutta)">The Telegraph</a></i> added that she "gets into the physicality of a pregnant woman with unfailing mastery".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <i>Kahaani</i> emerged as a major commercial success both at the domestic and international box office, with revenues of over <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1.04 billion</span> (US$15 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Vidya won a fourth consecutive Best Actress Award at Screen and a third Best Actress Award at Filmfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff12_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-ff12-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_struggles_.282013.E2.80.93present.29">Commercial struggles (2013–present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg"><img alt="Vidya Balan is smiling away from the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="374" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg/180px-Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg/270px-Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg/360px-Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Balan_in_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vidya at a promotional event for <i><a href="/wiki/Shaadi_Ke_Side_Effects" title="Shaadi Ke Side Effects">Shaadi Ke Side Effects</a></i> in 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After completing the duties of a jury member at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2013 Cannes Film Festival">2013 Cannes Film Festival</a>, Vidya starred opposite <a href="/wiki/Emraan_Hashmi" title="Emraan Hashmi">Emraan Hashmi</a> as a boisterous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjabi_people" title="Punjabi people">Punjabi woman</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Ghanchakkar_(film)" title="Ghanchakkar (film)">Ghanchakkar</a></i>, a comic-thriller from director Raj Kumar Gupta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannes_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-cannes-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Critics were unenthusiastic about the film and it earned little at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Vidya then provided the voice of <a href="/wiki/Draupadi" title="Draupadi">Draupadi</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Mahabharat_(2013_film)" title="Mahabharat (2013 film)">Mahabharat</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">3D animation film</a> based on the Indian epic <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">of the same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The romantic comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Shaadi_Ke_Side_Effects" title="Shaadi Ke Side Effects">Shaadi Ke Side Effects</a></i> was Vidya's first film release of 2014. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Saket_Chaudhary" title="Saket Chaudhary">Saket Chaudhary</a> and co-starring <a href="/wiki/Farhan_Akhtar" title="Farhan Akhtar">Farhan Akhtar</a>, the film tells the story of a married couple who face a series of comic events after the birth of their first child. Critics found the film to be a "bit overstretched", but praised both Akhtar and Vidya's performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Also that year, Vidya featured as the host of <i>No More Kamzor</i>, a television special on women empowerment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> She then starred in the comedy-drama <i><a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jasoos" title="Bobby Jasoos">Bobby Jasoos</a></i>, which saw her play the eponymous role of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyderabadi" title="Hyderabadi">Hyderabadi</a> woman aspiring to be a detective. Vidya was drawn to the idea of playing a female detective, and identified with the character's struggle to "do something unusual" in life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The role required her to sport twelve elaborate disguises, and she trained with a language coach to adopt a Hyderabadi accent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Saumil Gandhi of <i><a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Mirror" title="Mumbai Mirror">Mumbai Mirror</a></i> wrote that Vidya's "effervescence rubs off on the proceedings and gives it an energy that drives the film".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> However, both <i>Shaadi Ke Side Effects</i> and <i>Bobby Jasoos</i> failed to find a wide audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Vidya reteamed with Hashmi in the <a href="/wiki/Mohit_Suri" title="Mohit Suri">Mohit Suri</a>-directed romantic drama <i><a href="/wiki/Hamari_Adhuri_Kahani" title="Hamari Adhuri Kahani">Hamari Adhuri Kahani</a></i>. Penned by <a href="/wiki/Mahesh_Bhatt" title="Mahesh Bhatt">Mahesh Bhatt</a>, the film tells the story of Vasudha, a single mother trapped in an abusive marriage, who has an extra-marital affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Shubha Shetty-Saha of <i><a href="/wiki/Mid_Day" title="Mid Day">Mid Day</a></i> reviewed, "Vidya Balan, a fine actress with thousand emotions fleeting across her lovely face, has shown us what she's capable of in her earlier movies. But here, saddled with a boring, outdated, weepy character, there was nothing much even she could do".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Vidya next took on the part of a police officer in <i><a href="/wiki/Te3n" title="Te3n">Te3n</a></i> (2016), a thriller inspired by the 2013 South Korean film <i><a href="/wiki/Montage_(2013_film)" title="Montage (2013 film)">Montage</a></i>, co-starring Amitabh Bachchan and <a href="/wiki/Nawazuddin_Siddiqui" title="Nawazuddin Siddiqui">Nawazuddin Siddiqui</a>. She was attracted to the idea of playing a "no-nonsense police inspector who commands much respect" and was particularly drawn to her character's "silent aggression".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-move_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-move-92">[92]</a></sup> NDTV's Saibal Chatterjee criticised the decision to bill Vidya's pivotal role as a special appearance and noted how much her presence benefited the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Rajeev Masand was critical of the film's predictable denouement, but wrote that Vidya "is reliably solid each time she’s on screen, raising her brow, curling her lip to effectively communicate more than words can".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> She then portrayed the actress <a href="/wiki/Geeta_Bali" title="Geeta Bali">Geeta Bali</a> in multiple songs for <i><a href="/wiki/Ekk_Albela" title="Ekk Albela">Ekk Albela</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Marathi_cinema" title="Marathi cinema">Marathi</a> language biopic of the actor-director <a href="/wiki/Bhagwan_Dada" title="Bhagwan Dada">Bhagwan Dada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-move_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-move-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya's final release of the year was Sujoy Ghosh's <i><a href="/wiki/Kahaani_2:_Durga_Rani_Singh" title="Kahaani 2: Durga Rani Singh">Kahaani 2: Durga Rani Singh</a></i>, a sequel <i>Kahaani</i>, although it narrated a different story. The film was highly anticipated, and critics believed that Vidya's recent spate of poorly received films would come to an end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <i>Kahaani 2</i>, however, was not as well-received as the first film, although Vidya received a Best Actress nomination at Filmfare for her portrayal of a <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a> survivor in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Raja Sen thought that despite being an engaging thriller the film's denouement was predictable, but added that "with tremendous commitment to the part, [Vidya] gives us a stirring performance free of vanity or obviousness" and praised her "knack for winning the audience over; when she gasps, we gasp".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of January 2017, Vidya has filmed for the role of a <a href="/wiki/Procuring_(prostitution)" title="Procuring (prostitution)">procurer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Srijit_Mukherji" title="Srijit Mukherji">Srijit Mukherji</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Begum_Jaan" title="Begum Jaan">Begum Jaan</a></i>, a Hindi language remake of the Bengali film <i><a href="/wiki/Rajkahini" title="Rajkahini">Rajkahini</a></i> (2015), which is a drama set in a brothel during the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition of India in 1947</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In addition, Vidya will play a radio jockey who anchors a relationship advice talk show in the romantic comedy <i>Tumhari Sulu</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life_and_off-screen_work">Personal life and off-screen work</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg"><img alt="Vidya Balan and Siddharth Roy Kapur are smiling at the camera." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="245" data-file-width="391" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg/260px-Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg/390px-Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Siddharth_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vidya and <a href="/wiki/Siddharth_Roy_Kapur" title="Siddharth Roy Kapur">Siddharth Roy Kapur</a> at their wedding ceremony in December 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mass media has often speculated about a romantic relationship between Vidya and her co-actors, but she has strongly denied these reports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In 2009, Vidya was involved in a controversy when she mentioned a previous relationship in which "caustic remarks" were made at her due to her weight. She said, "If someone who matters to you takes you down, it can break you. That someone whose approval mattered to me started to constantly find faults with me. At that point of time, it was important to walk away from that relationship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Though she refused to name the person, <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid</a> reports suggested that she was referring to Shahid Kapoor (her co-star in <i>Kismat Konnection</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Kapoor, however, denied the allegations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> During an interview in May 2012, Vidya announced that she was dating <a href="/wiki/Siddharth_Roy_Kapur" title="Siddharth Roy Kapur">Siddharth Roy Kapur</a>, the CEO of <a href="/wiki/UTV_Motion_Pictures" title="UTV Motion Pictures">UTV Motion Pictures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> On 14 December 2012, the couple were married in a private ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Bandra" title="Bandra">Bandra</a>, Mumbai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya is trained in <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">carnatic music</a> and briefly studied the dance forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bharatnatyam" title="Bharatnatyam">Bharatnatyam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kathak" title="Kathak">Kathak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Regarding her religious affiliations, Vidya said, "I am a person with a lot of faith and I have conversations [with God] all the time but I am not so religious in the conventional, organised sense".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> She practices vegetarianism and was listed as "India's hottest vegetarian" in polls conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA">PETA</a> in 2011 and 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Her weight fluctuations over the years have been the subject of substantial media coverage in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides acting in film, Vidya promotes humanitarian causes and supports charitable institutions. In March 2011, she endorsed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Earth_Hour" title="Earth Hour">Earth Hour</a> campaign in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> She campaigned for the cause of nutrition in India for <a href="/wiki/Child_In_Need_Institute" title="Child In Need Institute">Child In Need Institute</a> (CINI), a non-profit organisation based in Kolkata.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In September 2012, Vidya visited a village in <a href="/wiki/Mirzapur" title="Mirzapur">Mirzapur</a>, Uttar Pradesh, where she participated in a campaign to promote children's education and the empowerment of women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> For her attempts to empower women, Vidya was awarded The Prabha Khaitan Puraskar 2012 by the Calcutta Chamber of Commerce; she was the youngest recipient of the award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Vidya has also been appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> as their brand ambassador in the drive to improve the country's sanitary condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In August 2013, she served as the grand marshal of the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(India)" title="Independence Day (India)">India Day parade</a> held in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In September that year, she launched a technology-based learning platform for underprivileged children in the Thanapur village of Uttar Pradesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> On the occasion of <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">International Women's Day</a> in 2015, Vidya wrote an opinion column in <i>Hindustan Times</i> on the issues faced by women in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_image_and_artistry">Media image and artistry</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_(3).jpg"><img alt="Vidya Balan holds a ball in her hand at a soccer field." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="392" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg/180px-Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg/270px-Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg/360px-Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vidya_Balan_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vidya at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the success of <i>Parineeta</i> and <i>Lage Raho Munna Bhai</i>, Vidya's film roles were subject to wide critical analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vir_Sanghvi" title="Vir Sanghvi">Vir Sanghvi</a> noted that the films <i>Heyy Babyy</i> and <i>Kismat Konnection</i> were "strange films [...] in which she tried to pretend to be what she is not — a Bollywood bimbette."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-rules-12">[12]</a></sup> Vidya described that particular phase in her career as a "struggle to be someone else".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Due to the criticism that her film choices evoked, Vidya decided to choose roles that she "believed in" rather than choose by convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-men_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-men-127">[127]</a></sup> Members of the media have subsequently labelled her as "bold" and "daring" in her choices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-list_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-list-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her starring roles in <i>Heyy Babyy</i> and <i>Kismat Konnection</i> also led to considerable attention in the media for her "questionable wardrobe". Several publications listed her as the "worst dressed actress" and her costume designers attributed her failure to carry off western clothes due to her weight and body structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> She was later praised in the media for wearing <a href="/wiki/Sari" title="Sari">saris</a> at public events; designer <a href="/wiki/Niharika_Khan" title="Niharika Khan">Niharika Khan</a> explained, "Vidya's beauty lies in her curves. She's comfortable in her voluptuousness, and therefore in a sari."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Vidya has since been identified as defying "an anglicised idea of sexuality" and embody the idea of "raw Indian sexuality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-men_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-men-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>After portraying strong female protagonists in <i>Paa</i>, <i>Ishqiya</i>, <i>No One Killed Jessica</i>, <i>The Dirty Picture</i> and <i>Kahaani</i>, Vidya was credited in the media for pioneering a movement that breaks the stereotypical portrayal of heroines in Bollywood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The major commercial success of the latter two earned her the title of a "female hero"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hero_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hero-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and Kalpana Nair of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Post_(India)" title="First Post (India)">First Post</a></i> noted that with these two films Vidya spearheaded a change in the roles that were offered to actresses over thirty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Mayank_Shekhar" title="Mayank Shekhar">Mayank Shekhar</a> predicted, "Just a few smart male actors can completely change the face of a commercial, star-driven film industry. Looking at [...] Vidya Balan [...] it appears, that change could well originate from the leading lady instead."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/India_Today" title="India Today">India Today</a></i> featured her in their listing of the "25 Power Women" and noted that "she has toppled the all dominating hero, reducing him to a supporting role in a male dominated film industry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Vidya occupied the top slot in Rediff.com's annual listing of "Bollywood's Best Actress" for two consecutive years (2010–11).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-list_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-list-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> She also featured in the list for the years 2005, 2006, 2009, and 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In 2010, she featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Filmfare" title="Filmfare">Filmfare</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s listing of the "Women we love".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In 2012, the magazine <i>Verve</i> listed her as one of India's "Young Power Women" and wrote, "In a reel world peopled by <a href="/wiki/Size_zero" title="Size zero">size zero</a>-toned bodies and pretty-as-a-picture heroines, Vidya comes across as completely real and natural – a woman who has followed her own instincts and dared to live her destiny by being her own person and not morphing herself to fit into any conventional slot."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quote1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-quote1-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2014, Vidya was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Shri" title="Padma Shri">Padma Shri</a>, the fourth highest civilian award in India, for her contributions to the entertainment industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The following year, she received an honorary Doctor of Arts degree from <a href="/wiki/Rai_Foundation" title="Rai Foundation">Rai University</a>; the university also named a scholarship program for underprivileged girls after her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The chancellor of the university, Harbeen Arora said, "Among the league of iconic actors, Vidya is a pioneer in every way. Her films epitomise a distinct Indianness and a powerful womanhood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography_and_awards">Filmography and awards</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_filmography">Selected filmography</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vidya_Balan_filmography" title="Vidya Balan filmography">Vidya Balan filmography</a></div>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bhool_Bhulaiyaa" title="Bhool Bhulaiyaa">Bhool Bhulaiyaa</a></i> (2007)</li>

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Vidya_Balan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Vidya Balan">List of awards and nominations received by Vidya Balan</a></div>
<p>Among Vidya's film awards are a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="National Film Award for Best Actress">National Film Award for Best Actress</a> for <i>The Dirty Picture</i> (2011),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-national_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-national-70">[70]</a></sup> and five Filmfare Awards: <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Female_Debut" title="Filmfare Award for Best Female Debut">Best Female Debut</a> for <i>Parineeta</i> (2005),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldawards_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-oldawards-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> for <i>Paa</i> (2009),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldawards_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-oldawards-29">[29]</a></sup> <i>The Dirty Picture</i> (2011),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awards_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-awards-54">[54]</a></sup> and <i>Kahaani</i> (2012),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff12_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-ff12-78">[78]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Critics_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actress">Critics Award for Best Actress</a> for <i>Ishqiya</i> (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awards_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-awards-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
